style=""white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"">Language</th><td>English</td></tr><tr><th scope=""row"" style=""white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"">Budget</th><td>$300 million<sup id=""cite_ref-BoxOfficeMojo_2-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BoxOfficeMojo-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope=""row"" style=""white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"">Box office</th><td>$963.4 million<sup id=""cite_ref-BoxOfficeMojo_2-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BoxOfficeMojo-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><i><b>Pirates of the Caribbean: At World\'s End</b></i> is a 2007 American <a href=""/wiki/Epic_film"" title=""Epic film"">epic</a> <a href=""/wiki/Fantasy_film"" title=""Fantasy film"">fantasy</a> <a href=""/wiki/Swashbuckler_film"" title=""Swashbuckler film"">swashbuckler film</a> directed by <a href=""/wiki/Gore_Verbinski"" title=""Gore Verbinski"">Gore Verbinski</a>, the third installment in the <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean (film series)""><i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> film series</a> and the sequel to <i><a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest"">Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i> (2006). The plot follows <a href=""/wiki/Will_Turner"" title=""Will Turner"">Will Turner</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Elizabeth_Swann"" title=""Elizabeth Swann"">Elizabeth Swann</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Hector_Barbossa"" title=""Hector Barbossa"">Hector Barbossa</a>, and the crew of the <i><a href=""/wiki/Black_Pearl"" title=""Black Pearl"">Black Pearl</a></i> rescuing <a href=""/wiki/Jack_Sparrow"" title=""Jack Sparrow"">Captain Jack Sparrow</a> from <a href=""/wiki/Geography_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean#Davy_Jones&#39;_Locker"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Geography of Pirates of the Caribbean"">Davy Jones\' Locker</a>, then preparing to fight the <a href=""/wiki/East_India_Trading_Company"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""East India Trading Company"">East India Trading Company</a>, led by <a href=""/wiki/Cutler_Beckett"" title=""Cutler Beckett"">Cutler Beckett</a>, who controls <a href=""/wiki/Davy_Jones_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" title=""Davy Jones (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Davy Jones</a> and plans to extinguish <a href=""/wiki/Piracy"" title=""Piracy"">piracy</a> forever. It is the last film in the series to be directed by Verbinski. It was filmed in two shoots during 2005 and 2006, the former simultaneously with <i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i>. With an estimated production budget of $300 million, <i>Pirates of the Caribbean: At World\'s End</i> was the <a href=""/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_films"" title=""List of most expensive films"">most expensive film ever made</a> at the time of its release, even after adjusting for inflation. It is currently the fifth most expensive film ever made.\n</p><p><a href=""/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures"" title=""Walt Disney Pictures"">Walt Disney Pictures</a> released the film in the United States on May 25, 2007. Critical reviews were mixed; the film was praised for its performances, musical score, action scenes, humor, and special effects but was criticized for its plot and running time. Despite this, <i>At World\'s End</i> was a box office hit, becoming the <a href=""/wiki/2007_in_film#Highest-grossing_films"" title=""2007 in film"">highest-grossing film of 2007</a> with over $960 million. It was nominated at the <a href=""/wiki/80th_Academy_Awards"" title=""80th Academy Awards"">80th Academy Awards</a> for the <a href=""/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Makeup_and_Hairstyling"" title=""Academy Award for Best Makeup and Hairstyling"">Academy Award for Best Makeup</a> and the <a href=""/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects"" title=""Academy Award for Best Visual Effects"">Academy Award for Best Visual Effects</a>, which it lost to <i><a href=""/wiki/La_Vie_en_Rose_(film)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""La Vie en Rose (film)"">La Vie en Rose</a></i> and <i><a href=""/wiki/The_Golden_Compass_(film)"" title=""The Golden Compass (film)"">The Golden Compass</a></i>, respectively. A sequel, <i><a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides"">On Stranger Tides</a></i>, the first in the series to neither be directed by Verbinski nor star Bloom and Knightley, was released on May 20, 2011.\n</p>\n<div id=""toc"" class=""toc""><input type=""checkbox"" role=""button"" id=""toctogglecheckbox"" tocsection-13""><a href=""#Box_office""><span class=""tocnumber"">5.2</span> <span class=""toctext"">Box office</span></a></li>\n<li class=""toclevel-2 tocsection-14""><a href=""#Accolades""><span class=""tocnumber"">5.3</span> <span class=""toctext"">Accolades</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class=""toclevel-1 tocsection-15""><a href=""#Sequel""><span class=""tocnumber"">6</span> <span class=""toctext"">Sequel</span></a></li>\n<li class=""toclevel-1 tocsection-16""><a href=""#References""><span class=""tocnumber"">7</span> <span class=""toctext"">References</span></a></li>\n<li class=""toclevel-1 tocsection-17""><a href=""#External_links""><span class=""tocnumber"">8</span> <span class=""toctext"">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Plot"">Plot</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"" title=""Edit section: Plot"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In order to control the oceans, Lord <a href=""/wiki/Cutler_Beckett"" title=""Cutler Beckett"">Cutler Beckett</a> executes anyone associated with <a href=""/wiki/Piracy"" title=""Piracy"">piracy</a> in <a href=""/wiki/Port_Royal"" title=""Port Royal"">Port Royal</a> by ordering <a href=""/wiki/Davy_Jones_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" title=""Davy Jones (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Davy Jones</a> to destroy all pirate ships in the seas. Condemned prisoners sing ""<a href=""/wiki/Hoist_the_Colours"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hoist the Colours"">Hoist the Colours</a>"" to compel the nine Pirate Lords to convene at <a href=""/wiki/Shipwreck_Cove"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Shipwreck Cove"">Shipwreck Cove</a> to hold the <a href=""/wiki/Brethren_Court"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Brethren Court"">Brethren Court</a>. Because <a href=""/wiki/Jack_Sparrow"" title=""Jack Sparrow"">Captain Jack Sparrow</a>, Pirate Lord of the <a href=""/wiki/Caribbean_Sea"" title=""Caribbean Sea"">Caribbean Sea</a>, never named a successor before being dragged to <a href=""/wiki/Davy_Jones_locker"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Davy Jones locker"">Davy Jones locker</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Captain_Barbossa"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Captain Barbossa"">Captain Barbossa</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Will_Turner"" title=""Will Turner"">Will Turner</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Elizabeth_Swann"" title=""Elizabeth Swann"">Elizabeth Swann</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Tia_Dalma"" title=""Tia Dalma"">Tia Dalma</a>, and the crew of the <i><a href=""/wiki/Black_Pearl"" title=""Black Pearl"">Black Pearl</a></i> plot to rescue Jack. Traveling to <a href=""/wiki/Singapore"" title=""Singapore"">Singapore</a>, the crew meet <a href=""/wiki/Captain_Sao_Feng"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Captain Sao Feng"">Captain Sao Feng</a> (Pirate Lord of the <a href=""/wiki/South_China_Sea"" title=""South China Sea"">South China Sea</a>), who owns navigational charts to the Locker. Beckett\'s soldiers invade, but the crew escape. Will secretly promises to give Jack to Feng in return for the <i>Pearl</i>, which he will use to rescue his father <a href=""/wiki/Bootstrap_Bill_Turner"" title=""Bootstrap Bill Turner"">Bootstrap Bill Turner</a> from the <i><a href=""/wiki/Flying_Dutchman_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" title=""Flying Dutchman (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Flying Dutchman</a></i>.\n</p><p>The crew travels to the Locker and rescues Jack. The crew encounters many dead souls, including Elizabeth\'s father <a href=""/wiki/Weatherby_Swann"" title=""Weatherby Swann"">Governor Swann</a>, who was executed by Beckett. Tia Dalma reveals that the Goddess Calypso charged Davy Jones with the job to guide the souls of those who died at sea to the next world. Once every ten years he could come ashore to be with the woman he loved. But he corrupted his purpose and was cursed to become a monster. The soul of Governor Swann reveals that whoever kills Jones, by stabbing his disembodied heart, must take his place as the <i>Dutchman</i>\'s captain.\n</p><p>Returning to the living world, the <i>Pearl</i> stops at an island for fresh water, where the crew find the <a href=""/wiki/Kraken_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" title=""Kraken (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Kraken</a> lying dead on the beach, having been killed by Jones under orders from Beckett. They are then attacked by Sao Feng and Beckett\'s men. Through a complex series of deals, Elizabeth is handed over to Feng, who believes she is the goddess <a href=""/wiki/Calypso_(mythology)"" title=""Calypso (mythology)"">Calypso</a>, while the rest of the crew make for Shipwreck Cove aboard the <i>Pearl</i>. Jack throws Will off the ship as part of the plan to seize control of the <i>Dutchman</i>. Sao Feng tells Elizabeth that the first Brethren Court bound Calypso in human form after she betrayed her lover, Davy Jones. He plans to release her to defeat Beckett. Davy Jones attacks Feng\'s ship, the <i>Empress</i>, mortally wounding Feng in the process. Feng appoints Elizabeth his successor as Pirate Lord before dying. Elizabeth and the crew are locked in the brig of the <i>Dutchman</i>, where she finds Bootstrap Bill losing himself to the <i>Dutchman</i>\'s curse. In a moment of clarity he tells her that Will must not come, since by killing Jones he will bind himself to the ship. <a href=""/wiki/James_Norrington"" title=""James Norrington"">Admiral Norrington</a> frees Elizabeth and her new crew from the <i>Dutchman</i>, but is killed by Bootstrap Bill.\n</p><p>The <i>Black Pearl</i> arrives at Shipwreck Cove, where Barbossa attempts to persuade the Brethren Court to release Calypso. Davy Jones visits Tia Dalma in the <i>Pearl</i>\'s brig, revealing she is Calypso. Jack\'s father <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Captain_Teague"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters"">Captain Teague</a>, Keeper of the <a href=""/wiki/Pirate_Code"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pirate Code"">Pirate Code</a>, informs the Court that only an elected Pirate King can decide on going into battle. A vote is taken. To avoid a stalemate, Jack casts his vote for Elizabeth, making her King.\n</p><p>The Brethren Court and Beckett\'s fleets emerge for war. On a <a href=""/wiki/Sandbank"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Sandbank"">sandbank</a>, Elizabeth, Jack, Barbossa, Beckett, Jones, and Will <a href=""/wiki/Parley"" title=""Parley"">parley</a>, trading Will for Jack. Barbossa steals Jack\'s piece of eight, all of which are owned by the Pirate Lords and required to free Calypso. Barbossa frees Calypso, but when Will reveals it was Jones who betrayed her and made it possible for the first Court to imprison her, Calypso vanishes and summons an enormous <a href=""/wiki/Whirlpool"" title=""Whirlpool"">maelstrom</a>.\n</p><p>The <i>Pearl</i> and the <i>Dutchman</i> battle in the maelstrom. Elizabeth and Will are wed by Barbossa. On board the <i>Dutchman</i>, Jones and Jack engage in a duel for control of Davy Jones\' heart. Jones stabs Will, mortally wounding him. Jack gives up his chance for immortality and instead helps Will stab the heart, killing Jones, whose body falls into the maelstrom. Jack and Elizabeth escape the <i>Dutchman</i> as it is sucked into the maelstrom.\n</p><p>As Beckett\'s ship, the <i>Endeavour</i>, approaches to destroy the <i>Pearl</i>, the <i>Dutchman</i> rises from the sea, now captained by Will; the crew has been freed from Jones\' curse. Together, the two pirate ships destroy the <i>Endeavour</i>. A stunned Beckett goes down with his ship while his navy retreats. With Will now forever bound to escort souls lost at sea to the next world, he and Elizabeth bid farewell to each other on the beach of an abandoned island. Will departs on the <i>Dutchman</i>, leaving Elizabeth pregnant and with the chest containing his heart.\n</p><p>Jack and <a href=""/wiki/Joshamee_Gibbs"" title=""Joshamee Gibbs"">Joshamee Gibbs</a> discover Barbossa has stolen the <i>Black Pearl</i> again, but Jack planned ahead and stole Sao Feng\'s navigational charts. He departs from <a href=""/wiki/Tortuga_(Haiti)"" title=""Tortuga (Haiti)"">Tortuga</a> alone to <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides"">track down the mythical Fountain of Youth</a>.\n</p><p>In a <a href=""/wiki/Post-credits_scene"" title=""Post-credits scene"">post-credits scene</a>, set ten years later, Elizabeth and her son <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Henry_Turner"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters"">Henry</a> watch from a sea cliff as Will returns aboard the <i>Dutchman</i>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Cast"">Cast</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"" title=""Edit section: Cast"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable"">Main articles: <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_cast_members"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean cast members"">List of Pirates of the Caribbean cast members</a> and <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters"">characters</a></div>\n<ul><li><a href=""/wiki/Johnny_Depp"" title=""Johnny Depp"">Johnny Depp</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Jack_Sparrow"" title=""Jack Sparrow"">Jack Sparrow</a>: Sparrow and the <i>Black Pearl</i> have been dragged to <a href=""/wiki/Davy_Jones%27_Locker_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Davy Jones&#39; Locker (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Davy Jones\' Locker</a> by the <a href=""/wiki/Kraken_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" title=""Kraken (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Kraken</a>; he is trapped there until his former crew mounts a rescue party.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Geoffrey_Rush"" title=""Geoffrey Rush"">Geoffrey Rush</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Hector_Barbossa"" title=""Hector Barbossa"">Hector Barbossa</a>: Once <a href=""/wiki/First_mate"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""First mate"">first mate</a> of the <i>Black Pearl</i> under Jack\'s command before leading a mutiny, Barbossa has been resurrected by Tia Dalma to captain the rescue of Jack Sparrow. He was also needed for his ""piece of eight"" to free Calypso. Rush said that in the film, Barbossa becomes more of a cunning politician.<sup id=""cite_ref-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Depp said he was pleased he got more screentime with Rush than in the first film: ""We\'re like a couple of old ladies fighting over their knitting needles"".<sup id=""cite_ref-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Orlando_Bloom"" title=""Orlando Bloom"">Orlando Bloom</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Will_Turner"" title=""Will Turner"">Will Turner</a>: A young <a href=""/wiki/Blacksmith"" title=""Blacksmith"">blacksmith</a>-turned-pirate, the son of ""Bootstrap Bill"" Turner, and later the husband of Elizabeth Swann. Turner becomes Captain of <i>The Flying Dutchman</i> after the ritual is performed to save his life.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Keira_Knightley"" title=""Keira Knightley"">Keira Knightley</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Elizabeth_Swann"" title=""Elizabeth Swann"">Elizabeth Swann</a>: Governor Swann\xe2\x80\x99s daughter and Will Turner\'s fianc\xc3\xa9e. Having tricked Jack Sparrow into being swallowed by the Kraken to save herself and the <i><a href=""/wiki/Black_Pearl"" title=""Black Pearl"">Black Pearl</a></i> crew, she subsequently goes to his rescue. Swann becomes Captain of <i>The Empress</i> and Pirate Lord of the South China Seas as successor to Feng, and becomes the Pirate King by default as a result of the <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Bretheren_Court"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters"">Bretheren Court</a> vote.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Bill_Nighy"" title=""Bill Nighy"">Bill Nighy</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Davy_Jones_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" title=""Davy Jones (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Davy Jones</a>: Malevolent ruler of the ocean realm, Captain of <i>The Flying Dutchman</i>. With his heart captured by James Norrington, he is now enslaved to Cutler Beckett who commanded him to kill the <a href=""/wiki/Kraken_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)"" title=""Kraken (Pirates of the Caribbean)"">Kraken</a> (""your pet""), and now serves the East India Trading Company, though he remains volatile and makes life difficult for the marines policing him.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Tom_Hollander"" title=""Tom Hollander"">Tom Hollander</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Cutler_Beckett"" title=""Cutler Beckett"">Cutler Beckett</a>: A powerful chairman of the <a href=""/wiki/East_India_Company"" title=""East India Company"">East India Trading Co.</a> and now armed with a mandate from the King and in possession of Davy Jones\' heart, Beckett attempts to control the world\'s oceans for the sake of sustainable business - and with it, the end of piracy.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Kevin_R._McNally"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Kevin R. McNally"">Kevin R. McNally</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Joshamee_Gibbs"" title=""Joshamee Gibbs"">Joshamee Gibbs</a>: Jack\'s loyal, if superstitious, first mate.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Jack_Davenport"" title=""Jack Davenport"">Jack Davenport</a> as <a href=""/wiki/James_Norrington"" title=""James Norrington"">James Norrington</a>: Promoted to the rank of <a href=""/wiki/Admiral"" title=""Admiral"">admiral</a> in return for giving Beckett Jones\' heart, he has allied himself with Beckett and the Company, although he still cares for Elizabeth, his former fianc\xc3\xa9e, and finds himself torn between his duty and his growing dislike for Beckett.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Jonathan_Pryce"" title=""Jonathan Pryce"">Jonathan Pryce</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Weatherby_Swann"" title=""Weatherby Swann"">Weatherby Swann</a>: Governor of Port Royal and father to Elizabeth Swann, he is now trapped in Beckett\'s service.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Lee_Arenberg"" title=""Lee Arenberg"">Lee Arenberg</a> and <a href=""/wiki/Mackenzie_Crook"" title=""Mackenzie Crook"">Mackenzie Crook</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Pintel_and_Ragetti"" title=""Pintel and Ragetti"">Pintel and Ragetti</a>: A mischievous and eccentric duo, part of Jack\'s crew.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/David_Bailie"" title=""David Bailie"">David Bailie</a> as Cotton: Jack\'s loyal mute crewman who returns again to join the quest to bring back Sparrow.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Stellan_Skarsg%C3%A5rd"" title=""Stellan Skarsg\xc3\xa5rd"">Stellan Skarsg\xc3\xa5rd</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Bootstrap_Bill_Turner"" title=""Bootstrap Bill Turner"">Bootstrap Bill Turner</a>: Will\'s father, cursed to serve an eternity aboard Davy Jones\' ship <i>The Flying Dutchman</i>. As he slowly loses hope, he also loses his humanity to the ship, and becomes mentally confused, barely recognizing his own son in the second half of the film.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Chow_Yun-fat"" title=""Chow Yun-fat"">Chow Yun-fat</a> as <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Sao_Feng"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters"">Sao Feng</a>: Pirate Lord of the <a href=""/wiki/South_China_Sea"" title=""South China Sea"">South China Sea</a>, he captains the Chinese ship <i>The Empress</i> and has a poor history with Sparrow. He is reluctant to aid in his rescue from Davy Jones\' Locker. ""Sao Feng"" (<span lang=""zh-hant""><a href=""https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%98%AF"" class=""extiw"" title=""wikt:\xe5\x98\xaf"">\xe5\x98\xaf</a><a href=""https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%A2%A8"" class=""extiw"" title=""wikt:\xe9\xa2\xa8"">\xe9\xa2\xa8</a></span>) means ""Howling Wind"" in Chinese. Chow was confirmed to be playing Feng in July 2005 while production of the second film was on hiatus.<sup id=""cite_ref-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Chow relished playing the role, even helping out crew members with props.<sup id=""cite_ref-Empire_6-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Empire-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Naomie_Harris"" title=""Naomie Harris"">Naomie Harris</a> as <a href=""/wiki/Tia_Dalma"" title=""Tia Dalma"">Tia Dalma</a>/<a href=""/wiki/Calypso_(mythology)"" title=""Calypso (mythology)"">Calypso</a>: An <a href=""/wiki/Obeah"" title=""Obeah"">obeah</a> witch who travels with the <i>Black Pearl</i> crew to rescue Jack; she also raised Barbossa from the dead at the conclusion of <i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i> and has a mysterious past connection to Davy Jones.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Martin_Klebba"" title=""Martin Klebba"">Martin Klebba</a> as Marty: Jack\'s dwarf crewman who also joins the quest to bring back Sparrow.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/David_Schofield_(actor)"" title=""David Schofield (actor)"">David Schofield</a> as Mr. Mercer: Lord Beckett\'s henchman, assigned to hold Davy Jones\' leash aboard the <i>Dutchman</i>.</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Keith_Richards"" title=""Keith Richards"">Keith Richards</a> as <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Captain_Teague"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters"">Edward Teague</a>: Keeper of the <a href=""/wiki/Pirate%27s_Code"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pirate&#39;s Code"">Pirata Codex</a> for the Brethren Court and Jack Sparrow\'s father. The other pirate lords are visibly terrified of him. Richards, who partially inspired Depp\'s portrayal of Sparrow,<sup id=""cite_ref-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> was meant to appear in <i>Dead Man\'s Chest</i>, but there was no room for him in the story,<sup id=""cite_ref-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> as well as his being tied up with a <a href=""/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones"" title=""The Rolling Stones"">Rolling Stones</a> tour. He almost missed filming a scene in <i>At World\'s End</i>, following injuries sustained by falling out of a tree.<sup id=""cite_ref-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In June 2006, Verbinski finally managed to make room in Richards\' schedule to shoot that September.<sup id=""cite_ref-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-10"">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Greg_Ellis_(actor)"" title=""Greg Ellis (actor)"">Greg Ellis</a> as <a href=""/wiki/List_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_characters#Lieutenant/Lieutenant_Commander_Theodore_Groves"" title=""List of Pirates of the Caribbean characters"">Theodore Groves</a>: The second-in-command to Lord Beckett.</li>\n<li>Lauren Maher and <a href=""/wiki/Vanessa_Branch"" title=""Vanessa Branch"">Vanessa Branch</a> as Scarlett and Giselle</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Angus_Barnett"" title=""Angus Barnett"">Angus Barnett</a> and Giles New as Mullroy and Murtogg</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Reggie_Lee_(actor)"" title=""Reggie Lee (actor)"">Reggie Lee</a> as Tai Huang</li>\n<li><a href=""/wiki/Dominic_Scott_Kay"" title=""Dominic Scott Kay"">Dominic Scott Kay</a> as Young Henry Turner: the son of Will Turner and Elizabeth Swann. Scott Kay was credited as Young William Turner, and was retroactively named Young Henry Turner following the release of <i><a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Men_Tell_No_Tales"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Men Tell No Tales"">Dead Men Tell No Tales</a></i>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Production"">Production</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"" title=""Edit section: Production"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Development"">Development</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"" title=""Edit section: Development"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable"">See also: <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest#Production"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest"">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man\'s Chest \xe2\x80\x93 Production</a></div>\n<div class=""quotebox pullquote floatright"" style=""width:30%;&#32;;""><style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r887775652"">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:""Times New Roman"",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:"" \xe2\x80\x9c "";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:""Times New Roman"",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:"" \xe2\x80\x9d "";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class=""quotebox-quote left-aligned"" style="""">""I felt it important that the third film was the end of an era &#8212; like in a <a href=""/wiki/Postmodern"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Postmodern"">postmodern</a> <a href=""/wiki/Western_(genre)"" title=""Western (genre)"">western</a> where the railroad comes and the gunfighter is extinct. It seemed that we had an opportunity to take a look at a world where the legitimate has become corrupt and there is no place for honest thieves in that society, so you have darker issues and a little melancholy. The myths are dying. That seemed a great theme with which to complete the trilogy.""</div>\n<p><cite class=""left-aligned"" style="""">\xe2\x80\x94<a href=""/wiki/Gore_Verbinski"" title=""Gore Verbinski"">Gore Verbinski</a><sup id=""cite_ref-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Following <i><a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl"">The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></i><span class=""nowrap"" style=""padding-left:0.1em;"">&#39;</span>s success in 2003, the cast and crew signed on for two sequels to be shot back-to-back.<sup id=""cite_ref-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> For the third film, director <a href=""/wiki/Gore_Verbinski"" title=""Gore Verbinski"">Gore Verbinski</a> wanted to return the tone to that of a character piece after using the second film to keep the plot moving.<sup id=""cite_ref-Empire_6-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Empire-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Inspired by the <a href=""/wiki/Brethren_of_the_Coast"" title=""Brethren of the Coast"">real-life confederation of pirates</a>, Elliott and Rossio looked at historical figures and created fictional characters from them to expand the scope beyond the main cast.<sup id=""cite_ref-13"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Finally embellishing their mythology, <a href=""/wiki/Calypso_(mythology)"" title=""Calypso (mythology)"">Calypso</a> was introduced, going full circle to Barbossa\'s mention of ""heathen gods"" that created the curse in the first film.<sup id=""cite_ref-14"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-14"">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Filming"">Filming</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"" title=""Edit section: Filming"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Parts of the third film were shot during location filming of <i><a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest"">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i>, a long shoot which finished on March 1, 2006.<sup id=""cite_ref-15"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> During August 2005, the <a href=""/wiki/Singapore"" title=""Singapore"">Singapore</a> sequence was shot. The set was built on Stage 12 of the <a href=""/wiki/Universal_Studios_Hollywood"" title=""Universal Studios Hollywood"">Universal Studios</a> backlot, and comprised 40 structures within an 80 by 130-foot (24 by 40-m) tank that was <span class=""frac nowrap"">3<span class=""visualhide"">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span> feet (1.1&#160;m) deep. As <a href=""/wiki/18th_century"" title=""18th century"">18th century</a> Singapore is not a well-documented era, the filmmakers chose to use an <a href=""/wiki/Expressionism"" title=""Expressionism"">Expressionist</a> style based on Chinese and <a href=""/wiki/Malaysia"" title=""Malaysia"">Malaysian</a> cities of the same period. The design of the city was also intended by Verbinski to parody <a href=""/wiki/Spa"" title=""Spa"">spa</a> culture, with fungi growing throughout the set. Continuing this natural feel, the floorboards of Sao Feng\'s bathhouse had to be cut by hand, and real humidity was created by the combination of gallons of water and the lighting equipment on the set.<sup id=""cite_ref-16"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Filming resumed on August 3, 2006 at the <a href=""/wiki/Bonneville_Salt_Flats"" title=""Bonneville Salt Flats"">Bonneville Salt Flats</a> in <a href=""/wiki/Utah"" title=""Utah"">Utah</a><sup id=""cite_ref-17"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> for 70 days off the California coast, as all the shooting required in the Caribbean had been conducted in 2005.<sup id=""cite_ref-18"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-18"">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href=""/wiki/Geography_of_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean#Davy_Jones&#39;_Locker"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Geography of Pirates of the Caribbean"">Davy Jones\' Locker</a> was shot at Utah, and it was shot in a <a href=""/wiki/Monochromatic"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monochromatic"">monochromatic</a> way to represent its different feeling from the usual colorful environment of a pirate.<sup id=""cite_ref-Deck_19-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Deck-19"">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The climactic battle was shot in a former air hangar at <a href=""/wiki/Palmdale,_California"" title=""Palmdale, California"">Palmdale, California</a>,<sup id=""cite_ref-20"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> where the cast had to wear wetsuits underneath their costumes on angle-tipped ships. The water-drenched set was kept in freezing temperatures, to make sure bacteria did not come inside and infect the crew.<sup id=""cite_ref-21"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A second unit was shot at <a href=""/wiki/Niagara_Falls"" title=""Niagara Falls"">Niagara Falls</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-22"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <a href=""/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic"" title=""Industrial Light &amp; Magic"">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a> did 750 effects shots, while <a href=""/wiki/Digital_Domain"" title=""Digital Domain"">Digital Domain</a> also took on 300. They spent just five months finishing the special effects. The film posed numerous challenges in creating water-based effects.<sup id=""cite_ref-23"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-23"">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Filming finished on December 12, 2006 in <a href=""/wiki/Molokai"" title=""Molokai"">Molokai</a>,<sup id=""cite_ref-Aloha_24-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Aloha-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and the first assembly cut was three hours.<sup id=""cite_ref-Rossio_25-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Rossio-25"">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Twenty minutes were removed, not including end credits, though producer <a href=""/wiki/Jerry_Bruckheimer"" title=""Jerry Bruckheimer"">Jerry Bruckheimer</a> maintained that the long running time was needed to make the final battle work in terms of build-up.<sup id=""cite_ref-26"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Music"">Music</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"" title=""Edit section: Music"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href=""/wiki/Hans_Zimmer"" title=""Hans Zimmer"">Hans Zimmer</a> composed the score, as he did for the previous films, and wrote the music for <i><a href=""/wiki/The_Simpsons_Movie"" title=""The Simpsons Movie"">The Simpsons Movie</a></i> at the same time. Zimmer composed eight new motifs, including a new love theme for the <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End_(soundtrack)"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End (soundtrack)""><i>At World\'s End</i> soundtrack</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Aloha_24-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Aloha-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He scored scenes as the editors began work, so as to influence their choice of cutting to the music. Gore Verbinski helped on the score. He played the <a href=""/wiki/Ennio_Morricone"" title=""Ennio Morricone"">Ennio Morricone</a>-influenced guitar music in the parley scene between Barbossa, Sparrow, Elizabeth and Will, Davy Jones, and Cutler Beckett. <sup id=""cite_ref-27"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He also co-wrote the song ""<a href=""/wiki/Hoist_the_Colours"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hoist the Colours"">Hoist the Colours</a>"" with Zimmer.<sup id=""cite_ref-28"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Release"">Release</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"" title=""Edit section: Release"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:222px;""><a href=""/wiki/File:Keith_Richards.jpg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Keith_Richards.jpg/220px-Keith_Richards.jpg"" decoding=""async"" width=""220"" height=""215"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Keith_Richards.jpg 1.5x"" data-file-width=""250"" data-file-height=""244"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""/wiki/File:Keith_Richards.jpg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div><a href=""/wiki/Keith_Richards"" title=""Keith Richards"">Keith Richards</a>, who plays Jack\'s father <a href=""/wiki/Captain_Teague"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Captain Teague"">Captain Teague</a>, at the premiere.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href=""/wiki/Premiere"" title=""Premiere"">world premiere</a> of <i>At World\'s End</i> was held on May 19, 2007 at <a href=""/wiki/Disneyland"" title=""Disneyland"">Disneyland</a>, home of the ride that inspired the film and where the first two films in the trilogy debuted. Disneyland offered the general public a chance to attend the premiere through the sale of tickets, priced at $1,500 per ticket, with proceeds going to the <a href=""/wiki/Make-a-Wish_Foundation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Make-a-Wish Foundation"">Make-a-Wish Foundation</a> charity.<sup id=""cite_ref-29"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-29"">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Just a few weeks before the film\'s release, <a href=""/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures"" title=""Walt Disney Pictures"">Walt Disney Pictures</a> decided to move the United States opening of <i>At World\'s End</i> from screenings Friday, May 25, 2007 to Thursday at 8 PM, May 24, 2007.<sup id=""cite_ref-30"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-30"">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The film opened in 4,362 theaters domestically, beating <i><a href=""/wiki/Spider-Man_3"" title=""Spider-Man 3"">Spider-Man 3</a></i><span class=""nowrap"" style=""padding-left:0.1em;"">&#39;</span>s theater opening record by 110 (this record was surpassed by <i><a href=""/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)"" title=""The Dark Knight (film)"">The Dark Knight</a></i> the following year).<sup id=""cite_ref-31"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-31"">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-32"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-32"">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Marketing"">Marketing</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"" title=""Edit section: Marketing"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After a muted publicity campaign, the trailer finally debuted at <a href=""/wiki/ShoWest"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""ShoWest"">ShoWest</a> 2007.<sup id=""cite_ref-33"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-33"">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> It was shown on March 18, 2007 at a special screening of <i><a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_The_Curse_of_the_Black_Pearl"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl"">Pirates of the Caribbean: The Curse of the Black Pearl</a></i> named ""Pirates Ultimate Fan Event"", and was then shown on March 19 during <i><a href=""/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._TV_series)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dancing with the Stars (U.S. TV series)"">Dancing with the Stars</a></i>, before it debuted online.<sup id=""cite_ref-34"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-34"">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Action figures by <a href=""/wiki/National_Entertainment_Collectibles_Association"" title=""National Entertainment Collectibles Association"">NECA</a> were released in late April.<sup id=""cite_ref-35"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-35"">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href=""/wiki/Board_game"" title=""Board game"">Board games</a> such as a Collector\'s Edition <a href=""/wiki/Chess"" title=""Chess"">Chess</a> Set, a <a href=""/wiki/Monopoly_(game)"" title=""Monopoly (game)"">Monopoly</a> Game, and a Pirates Dice Game (<a href=""/wiki/Liar%27s_Dice"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Liar&#39;s Dice"">Liar\'s dice</a>) were also released. <a href=""/wiki/Corgi_International_Limited#Master_Replicas"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Corgi International Limited"">Master Replicas</a> made sculptures of characters and replicas of jewellery and the Dead Man\'s Chest.<sup id=""cite_ref-36"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-36"">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> A <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End_(video_game)"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End (video game)"">video game</a> with the same title as the film was released on May 22, 2007 on <a href=""/wiki/Xbox_360"" title=""Xbox 360"">Xbox 360</a>, <a href=""/wiki/PlayStation_3"" title=""PlayStation 3"">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Wii"" title=""Wii"">Wii</a>, <a href=""/wiki/PlayStation_Portable"" title=""PlayStation Portable"">PSP</a>, <a href=""/wiki/PlayStation_2"" title=""PlayStation 2"">PlayStation 2</a>, <a href=""/wiki/Personal_computer"" title=""Personal computer"">PC</a>, and <a href=""/wiki/Nintendo_DS"" title=""Nintendo DS"">Nintendo DS</a> formats.<sup id=""cite_ref-37"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-37"">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End_(soundtrack)"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End (soundtrack)"">The soundtrack</a> and <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End_Remixes"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: At World&#39;s End Remixes"">its remix</a> were also released on May 22.\n</p>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Censorship"">Censorship</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"" title=""Edit section: Censorship"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At least one nation\'s official <a href=""/wiki/Censorship"" title=""Censorship"">censors</a> ordered scenes cut from the film. According to <a href=""/wiki/Xinhua"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Xinhua"">Xinhua</a>, the state news agency of the <a href=""/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""People&#39;s Republic of China"">People\'s Republic of China</a>, ten minutes of footage containing <a href=""/wiki/Chow_Yun-fat"" title=""Chow Yun-fat"">Chow Yun-fat</a>\'s portrayal of Singaporean pirate <a href=""/wiki/Sao_Feng"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Sao Feng"">Sao Feng</a> were trimmed from versions of the film which may be shown in China. Chow is onscreen for twenty minutes in the uncensored theatrical release of the film. No official reason for the censorship was given, but unofficial sources within China have indicated that the character gave a negative and stereotypical portrayal of Chinese people.<sup id=""cite_ref-38"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-38"">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Home_media"">Home media</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"" title=""Edit section: Home media"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The film was released on DVD and Blu-Ray on November 19, 2007 in the UK and December 4, 2007 in the United States and Canada. The 2-Disc Limited Edition DVD was in continuous circulation until it stopped on September 30, 2008. In contrast, the Blu-ray Disc release, containing all of the features from the 2-Disc DVD version (including some original scenes from the theatrical release, but excluding the writer\'s <a href=""/wiki/Audio_commentary"" title=""Audio commentary"">commentary</a>) is still widely available. The initial Blu-ray Disc release was misprinted on the back of the box as <a href=""/wiki/1080i"" title=""1080i"">1080i</a>, although Disney confirmed it to be <a href=""/wiki/1080p"" title=""1080p"">1080p</a>. Disney decided not to recall the misprinted units, but to fix the error on subsequent printings.<sup id=""cite_ref-39"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-39"">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> DVD sales brought in $296,043,871 in revenue, marking the best-selling DVD of 2007, although it ranks second in terms of units sold (14,505,271) behind <i><a href=""/wiki/Transformers_(film)"" title=""Transformers (film)"">Transformers</a></i> (16,234,195).<sup id=""cite_ref-The-Numbers_40-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-The-Numbers-40"">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <i>At World\'s End</i> had its television premiere in the UK on <a href=""/wiki/Boxing_Day"" title=""Boxing Day"">Boxing Day</a> 2009 on <a href=""/wiki/BBC_One"" title=""BBC One"">BBC One</a> at 19:30,<sup id=""cite_ref-41"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-41"">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-42"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-42"">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and was watched by 6.06 million viewers.<sup id=""cite_ref-43"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-43"">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Reception"">Reception</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"" title=""Edit section: Reception"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Critical_response"">Critical response</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"" title=""Edit section: Critical response"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On review aggregation website <a href=""/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes"" title=""Rotten Tomatoes"">Rotten Tomatoes</a> the film has an approval rating of 44% based on 224 reviews, with an average rating of 5.4/10. The site\'s critical consensus reads, ""<i>POTC: AWE</i> provides the thrilling action scenes, but mixes in too many characters with too many incomprehensible plot threads.""<sup id=""cite_ref-44"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-44"">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> At <a href=""/wiki/Metacritic"" title=""Metacritic"">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a weighted average rating to reviews, the film received an average score of 50 out of 100, based on 36 critics, indicating ""mixed or average reviews"".<sup id=""cite_ref-45"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-45"">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Audiences polled by <a href=""/wiki/CinemaScore"" title=""CinemaScore"">CinemaScore</a> gave the film an average grade of ""A\xe2\x80\x93"" on an A+ to F scale.<sup id=""cite_ref-CinemaScore_46-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-CinemaScore-46"">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Reviewer Alex Billington noted, ""This is just how the film industry works nowadays; critics give bad opinions, the public usually has a differing opinion, and all is well in the world of Hollywood since the studios made their millions anyway.""<sup id=""cite_ref-47"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-47"">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Drew_McWeeny&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Drew McWeeny (page does not exist)"">Drew McWeeny</a> praised the film\'s complexity as giving it repeat-viewing value, and its conclusion as ""perhaps the most canny move it makes.""<sup id=""cite_ref-48"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-48"">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Todd Gilchrist found the story too similar to other cinematic trilogies such as <i><a href=""/wiki/Star_Wars"" title=""Star Wars"">Star Wars</a></i>, but praised the production values.<sup id=""cite_ref-49"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-49"">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Brian Lowry felt that ""unlike last year\'s bloated sequel, it at least possesses some semblance of a destination, making it slightly more coherent - if no less numbing during the protracted finale.""<sup id=""cite_ref-50"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-50"">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href=""/wiki/Total_Film"" title=""Total Film"">Total Film</a></i> praised the performances but complained that the twists and exposition made it hard to care for the characters.<sup id=""cite_ref-51"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-51"">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Edward Douglas liked the film but had issues with its pacing,<sup id=""cite_ref-52"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-52"">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> while Blake Wright criticized the Davy Jones\' Locker and Calypso segments.<sup id=""cite_ref-53"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-53"">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> <a href=""/wiki/James_Berardinelli"" title=""James Berardinelli"">James Berardinelli</a> found it the weakest of the trilogy as ""the last hour offers adventure as rousing as anything provided in either of the previous installments... which doesn\'t account for the other 108 minutes of this gorged, self-indulgent, and uneven production.""<sup id=""cite_ref-54"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-54"">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <a href=""/wiki/Peter_Travers"" title=""Peter Travers"">Peter Travers</a> praised Richards and Rush but felt ""there can indeed be too much of a good thing,"" regarding Depp\'s character.<sup id=""cite_ref-55"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-55"">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Travers later declared the movie to be one of the worst films of the year.<sup id=""cite_ref-56"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-56"">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Colm Andrew of the <i><a href=""/wiki/Manx_Independent"" title=""Manx Independent"">Manx Independent</a></i> said the film was overall a disappointment and that ""the final showdown ... is a non-event and the repetitive swordplay and inane plot contrivances simply become boring by the end"".<sup id=""cite_ref-57"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-57"">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href=""/wiki/Richard_Roeper"" title=""Richard Roeper"">Richard Roeper</a> gave a positive review, saying ""Gore Verbinski and the stunt and special effects crews have created one of the most impressive blends of live-action work and CGI wizardry ever put on film,"" and believing it ""rarely drags and is almost always entertaining."" He praised the performances of the actors as one of the best things about the film.<sup id=""cite_ref-58"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-58"">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href=""/wiki/Chow_Yun-fat"" title=""Chow Yun-fat"">Chow Yun-fat</a>\'s character stirred a great deal of controversy with the Chinese press. <a href=""/w/index.php?title=Perry_Lam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Perry Lam (page does not exist)"">Perry Lam</a>, of Hong Kong cultural magazine, <i><a href=""/wiki/Muse_(Hong_Kong_magazine)"" title=""Muse (Hong Kong magazine)"">Muse</a></i>, found an offensive resemblance between Chow\'s character and <a href=""/wiki/Fu_Manchu"" title=""Fu Manchu"">Fu Manchu</a>: ""Now Fu Manchu has returned after an absence of 27 years in the Hollywood cinema; except that, in a nod to political correctness and marketing realities, he is no longer called Fu Manchu.""<sup id=""cite_ref-59"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-59"">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Box_office"">Box office</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"" title=""Edit section: Box office"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Pirates of the Caribbean: At World\'s End</i> earned $309,420,425 in North America and $654,000,000 in other countries, for a worldwide total of $963,420,425.<sup id=""cite_ref-BoxOfficeMojo_2-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BoxOfficeMojo-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Worldwide, it is the <a href=""/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films"" title=""List of highest-grossing films"">thirty-eighth-highest-grossing film</a>,<sup id=""cite_ref-60"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-60"">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> the <a href=""/wiki/2007_in_film"" title=""2007 in film"">highest-grossing film of 2007</a>,<sup id=""cite_ref-61"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-61"">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and the third-highest-grossing film in the <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean (film series)""><i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> series</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-POTC-series_62-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-POTC-series-62"">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Compared to its predecessor, it grossed far less at the North American box office, but more outside North America. Still, its worldwide earnings are more than $100 million below <i><a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man&#39;s Chest"">Dead Man\'s Chest</a></i><span class=""nowrap"" style=""padding-left:0.1em;"">&#39;</span>s.<sup id=""cite_ref-63"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-63"">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> During its worldwide opening weekend, it grossed $344.0 million, making it the seventh-largest opening.<sup id=""cite_ref-64"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-64"">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>North America</dt></dl>\n<p><i>At World\'s End</i> was released in a then-record 4,362 theaters in North America,<sup id=""cite_ref-65"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-65"">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> and was shown on around 11,500 screens, which is still an all-time record.<sup id=""cite_ref-66"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-66"">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On its first three-day weekend, it earned $114,732,820. It set a Memorial Day 4-day weekend record ($139,802,190), which it still retains. This record was previously held by <i><a href=""/wiki/X-Men:_The_Last_Stand"" title=""X-Men: The Last Stand"">X-Men: The Last Stand</a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-67"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-67"">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Including Thursday night previews, as well, <i>At World\'s End</i> earned $153,042,234 in 5 days,<sup id=""cite_ref-BOM_68-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BOM-68"">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and is the fourth-highest-grossing film of 2007.<sup id=""cite_ref-69"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-69"">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Among <i>May\'s Big Three</i> (<i><a href=""/wiki/Spider-Man_3"" title=""Spider-Man 3"">Spider-Man 3</a></i>, <i><a href=""/wiki/Shrek_the_Third"" title=""Shrek the Third"">Shrek 3</a></i> and <i>Pirates 3</i>),<sup id=""cite_ref-70"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-70"">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-71"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-71"">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> <i>Pirates 3</i> grossed the least both during its opening weekend<sup id=""cite_ref-72"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-72"">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and in total earnings.<sup id=""cite_ref-73"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-73"">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> However, this was mainly attributed to the fact that it was released third, after the other two films, so there was already too much competition.<sup id=""cite_ref-74"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-74"">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> It is also the second-highest-grossing film in the <i>Pirates</i> series.<sup id=""cite_ref-POTC-series_62-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-POTC-series-62"">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Outside North America</dt></dl>\n<p>It is the eighteenth-highest-grossing film, the sixth-largest film distributed by Disney,<sup id=""cite_ref-75"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-75"">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and the second-highest-grossing <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i> film.<sup id=""cite_ref-POTC-series_62-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-POTC-series-62"">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> During its opening weekend, it grossed an estimated $216.0 million, which stands as the sixth biggest opening outside North America.<sup id=""cite_ref-76"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-76"">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> It set opening-weekend records in South Korea with $16.7 million (surpassed by <i><a href=""/wiki/Transformers:_Dark_of_the_Moon"" title=""Transformers: Dark of the Moon"">Transformers: Dark of the Moon</a></i>),<sup id=""cite_ref-77"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-77"">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Russia, and the CIS with $14.0 million (first surpassed by <i><a href=""/wiki/The_Best_Movie"" title=""The Best Movie"">Samy luchshiy film</a></i>),<sup id=""cite_ref-78"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-78"">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and Spain with $11.9 million<sup id=""cite_ref-79"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-79"">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> (surpassed by <i><a href=""/wiki/The_Impossible_(2012_film)"" title=""The Impossible (2012 film)"">The Impossible</a></i>).<sup id=""cite_ref-80"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-80"">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> It dominated for three consecutive weekends at the box office outside North America.<sup id=""cite_ref-81"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-81"">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> By June 12, 2007, its 20th day of release, the film had grossed $500 million, breaking <i>Spider-Man 3\'</i>s record for reaching that amount the fastest.<sup id=""cite_ref-82"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-82"">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> This record was first overtaken by <i><a href=""/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)"" title=""Avatar (2009 film)"">Avatar</a></i> (15 days to $500 million).<sup id=""cite_ref-83"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-83"">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Its highest-grossing countries after North America are Japan, where it earned $91.1 million, and became the last Hollywood film to earn more than 10 billion yen before <i>Avatar</i>,<sup id=""cite_ref-84"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-84"">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and the UK, Ireland, Malta ($81.4 million), and Germany ($59.4 million).<sup id=""cite_ref-Box_Office_Mojo_85-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Box_Office_Mojo-85"">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Accolades"">Accolades</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14"" title=""Edit section: Accolades"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable"">See also: <a href=""/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_the_Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_film_series"" title=""List of accolades received by the Pirates of the Caribbean film series"">List of accolades received by the Pirates of the Caribbean film series</a></div>\n<p>At the <a href=""/wiki/80th_Academy_Awards"" title=""80th Academy Awards"">80th Academy Awards</a>, <i>Pirates of the Caribbean: At World\'s End</i> was nominated for two awards, <a href=""/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Makeup_and_Hairstyling"" title=""Academy Award for Best Makeup and Hairstyling"">Best Makeup</a> and <a href=""/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects"" title=""Academy Award for Best Visual Effects"">Best Visual Effects</a>. However, it did not win either of the two, losing the former to <i><a href=""/wiki/La_Vie_en_rose_(film)"" title=""La Vie en rose (film)"">La Vie en rose</a></i> and the latter to <i><a href=""/wiki/The_Golden_Compass_(film)"" title=""The Golden Compass (film)"">The Golden Compass</a></i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-86"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-86"">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the <a href=""/wiki/2008_MTV_Movie_Awards"" title=""2008 MTV Movie Awards"">2008 MTV Movie Awards</a>, the film was nominated for three awards, including one win: the Best Comedic Performance (Johnny Depp). At the <a href=""/wiki/34th_People%27s_Choice_Awards"" title=""34th People&#39;s Choice Awards"">34th People\'s Choice Awards</a>, it was nominated for five awards, including four wins: Favorite Movie, Favorite <a href=""/wiki/Threequel"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Threequel"">Threequel</a>, Favorite Male Movie Star (Johnny Depp) and Favorite Female Action Star (Keira Knightley).<sup id=""cite_ref-87"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-87"">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Also, at the <a href=""/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards"" title=""Teen Choice Awards"">Teen Choice Awards</a> it won <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)#Teen_Choice_Awards"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean (film series)"">five awards</a>, out of six nominations. Finally, at the <a href=""/wiki/2008_Kids%27_Choice_Awards"" title=""2008 Kids&#39; Choice Awards"">2008 Kids\' Choice Awards</a>, it achieved three nominations but won only the Favorite Movie Actor award (Johnny Depp). However, <a href=""/wiki/Orlando_Bloom"" title=""Orlando Bloom"">Orlando Bloom</a> was nominated for a <a href=""/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Awards"" title=""Golden Raspberry Awards"">Golden Raspberry Award</a> for <a href=""/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Supporting_Actor"" title=""Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Supporting Actor"">Worst Supporting Actor</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Sequel"">Sequel</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15"" title=""Edit section: Sequel"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable"">Main article: <a href=""/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides"" title=""Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides"">Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides</a></div>\n<h2><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""References"">References</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"" title=""Edit section: References"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class=""reflist"" style=""list-style-type: decimal;"">\n<div class=""mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns""><ol class=""references"">\n<li id=""cite_note-1""><span class=""mw-cite-backlink""><b><a href=""#cite_ref-1"">^</a></b></span> <span class=""reference-text""><cite class=""citation web""><a rel=""nofollow"" class=""external text"" href=""http://bbfc.co.uk/releases/pirates-caribbean-worlds-end-2007-0"">""Pirates of the Caribbean - At World\'s End""</a>. <a href=""/wiki/British_Board_of_Film_Classification"" title=""British Board of Film Classification"">British Board of Film Classification</a>.
